**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6`, `github.com/sg-evals/istio--2300e245`, `github.com/sg-evals/emissary--3bbdbe0f`

Find all concrete server implementations of the `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` gRPC interface across xDS control plane repositories.

## Background

The Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) is the primary xDS protocol for delivering configuration to Envoy proxies. The gRPC service is defined in the proto file `envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto`:

```protobuf
service AggregatedDiscoveryService {
  rpc StreamAggregatedResources(stream DiscoveryRequest)
    returns (stream DiscoveryResponse) {}

  rpc DeltaAggregatedResources(stream DeltaDiscoveryRequest)
    returns (stream DeltaDiscoveryResponse) {}
}
```

When compiled to Go, this generates a server interface `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` in the package `github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/discovery/v3`. Any struct that implements the methods of this interface acts as an xDS control plane server.

## Repositories

Three repositories are available under `/workspace/`:

- `/workspace/go-control-plane/` — envoyproxy/go-control-plane (Go xDS server SDK, reference implementations)
- `/workspace/istio/` — istio/istio (Istio control plane with Pilot xDS server)
- `/workspace/emissary/` — emissary-ingress/emissary (Envoy-based API gateway with xDS configuration server)

## Task

Find **all struct types** that implement the `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` interface across all three repositories. These are types that provide concrete implementations of:
- `StreamAggregatedResources(stream AggregatedDiscoveryService_StreamAggregatedResourcesServer) error`
- `DeltaAggregatedResources(stream AggregatedDiscoveryService_DeltaAggregatedResourcesServer) error`

For each implementor, record:
- `repo`: one of `envoyproxy/go-control-plane`, `istio/istio`, or `emissary-ingress/emissary`
- `file`: path relative to the repository root (e.g., `pkg/server/v3/server.go`)
- `struct_name`: the name of the struct type that implements the interface (e.g., `Server`, `DiscoveryServer`)

## Output

Write your results to `/workspace/implementors.json` as a JSON array:

```json
[
  {
    "repo": "envoyproxy/go-control-plane",
    "file": "pkg/server/v3/server.go",
    "struct_name": "Server"
  },
  {
    "repo": "istio/istio",
    "file": "pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go",
    "struct_name": "DiscoveryServer"
  }
]
```

## Inclusion Criteria

**Include:**
- Production server implementations (the main control plane servers)
- Test server implementations (mock servers, fake servers for testing)
- Partial implementations (types that implement at least one of the two methods)
- Embedded server types (if a struct embeds the interface but provides its own methods)

**Exclude:**
- The generated protobuf interface definition itself (in `*_grpc.pb.go` files)
- Pure interface embeddings without method implementations (e.g., `type X struct { AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer }` with no methods)
- Deprecated or commented-out implementations
- Vendor directory code
- Types that only **call** the server interface (clients), not implement it

since those are carried separately.\\n465: \\t}\\n466: \\n467: \\t// The configuration data that reaches us here arrives via two parallel paths that race each\\n468: \\t// other. The endpoint data comes in realtime directly from the golang watcher in the entrypoint\\n469: \\t// package. The cluster configuration comes from the python code. Either one can win which means\\n470: \\t// we might at times see endpoint data with no corresponding cluster and we might also see\\n471: \\t// clusters with no corresponding endpoint data. Both of these circumstances should be\\n472: \\t// transient.\\n473: \\t//\\n474: \\t// To produce a consistent configuration we do an outer join operation on the endpoint and\\n475: \\t// cluster configuration that we have at this moment. If there is no endpoint information for a\\n476: \\t// given cluster, we will synthesize an empty ClusterLoadAssignment.\\n477: \\t//\\n478: \\t// Note that a cluster not existing is very different to envoy than a cluster existing but\\n479: \\t// having an empty ClusterLoadAssignment. When envoy first discovers clusters it goes through a\\n480: \\t// warmup process to be sure the cluster is properly bootstrapped before routing traffic to\\n481: \\t// it. See here for more details:\\n482: \\t//\\n483: \\t// https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/arch_overview/upstream/cluster_manager.html?highlight=cluster%20warming\\n484: \\t//\\n485: \\t// For this reason if there is no endpoint data for the cluster we will synthesize an empty\\n486: \\t// ClusterLoadAssignment rather than filtering out the cluster. This avoids triggering the\\n487: \\t// warmup sequence in scenarios where the endpoint data for a cluster is really flapping into\\n488: \\t// and out of existence.     "content": "1: package ambex\n2: \n3: /**********************************************\n4:  * ambex: Ambassador Experimental ADS server\n5:  *\n6:  * Here's the deal.\n7:  *\n8:  * go-control-plane, several different classes manage this stuff:\n9:  *\n10:  * - The root of the world is a SnapshotCache.\n11:  *   - import github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/pkg/cache/v3, then refer\n12:  *     to cache.SnapshotCache.\n13:  *   - A collection of internally consistent configuration objects is a\n14:  *     Snapshot (cache.Snapshot).\n15:  *   - Snapshots are collected in the SnapshotCache.\n16:  *   - A given SnapshotCache can hold configurations for multiple Envoys,\n17:  *     identified by the Envoy 'node ID', which must be configured for the\n18:  *     Envoy.\n19:  * - The SnapshotCache can only hold go-control-plane configuration objects,\n20:  *   so you have to build these up to hand to the SnapshotCache.\n21:  * - The gRPC stuff is handled by a Server.\n22:  *   - import github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/pkg/server, then refer\n23:  *     to server.Server.\n24:  *   - Our runManagementServer (largely ripped off from the go-control-plane\n25:  *     tests) gets this running. It takes a SnapshotCache (cleverly called a\n26:  *     \"config\" for no reason I understand) and a gRPCServer as arguments.\n27:  *   - _ALL_ the gRPC madness is handled by the Server, with the assistance\n28:  *     of the methods in a callback object.\n29:  * - Once the Server is running, Envoy can open a gRPC stream to it.\n30:  *   - On connection, Envoy will get handed the most recent Snapshot that\n31:  *     the Server's SnapshotCache knows about.\n32:  *   - Whenever a newer Snapshot is added to the SnapshotCache, that Snapshot\n33:  *     will get sent to the Envoy.\n34:  * - We manage the SnapshotCache by loading envoy configuration from\n35:  *   json and/or protobuf files on disk.\n36:  *   - By default when we get a SIGHUP, we reload configuration.\n37:  *   - When \n169: \t// We'll keep $AMBASSADOR_AMBEX_SNAPSHOT_COUNT snapshots. our config\n234: var decoders = map[string](func([]byte, proto.Message) error){\n235: \t\".json\": protojson.Unmarshal,\n236: \t\".pb\":   prototext.Unmarshal,\n237: }\n238: \n239: func isDecodable(name string) bool {\n240: \tif strings.HasPrefix(name, \".\") {\n241: \t\treturn false\n242: \t}\n243: \n244: \text := filepath.Ext(name)\n245: \t_, ok := decoders[ext]\n246: \treturn ok\n247: }\n248: \n249: // Not sure if there is a better way to do this, but we cast to this\n250: // so we can call the generated Validate method.\n251: type Validatable interface {\n252: \tproto.Message\n253: \tValidate() error\n254: }\n255: \n256: func Decode(ctx context.Context, name string) (proto.Message, error) {\n257: \tany := &anypb.Any{}\n258: \tcontents, err := ioutil.ReadFile(name)\n259: \tif err != nil {\n260: \t\treturn nil, err\n261: \t}\n262: \n263: \text := filepath.Ext(name)\n264: \tdecoder := decoders[ext]\n265: \terr = decoder(contents, any)\n266: \tif err != nil {\n267: \t\treturn nil, err\n268: \t}\n269: \n270: \tm, err := any.UnmarshalNew()\n271: \tif err != nil {\n272: \t\treturn nil, err\n273: \t}\n274: \n275: \tv := m.(Validatable)\n276: \n277: \tif err := v.Validate(); err != nil {\n278: \t\treturn nil, err\n279: \t}\n280: \tdlog.Infof(ctx, \"Loaded file %s\", name)\n281: \treturn v, nil\n282: }\n283: \n284: // Observability:\n285: //\n286: // These \"expanded\" snapshots make the snapshots we log easier to read: basically,\n287: // instead of just indexing by Golang types, make the JSON marshal with real names.\n288: type v3ExpandedSnapshot struct {\n289: \tEndpoints ecp_v3_cache.Resources `json:\"endpoints\"`\n290: \tClusters  ecp_v3_cache.Resources `json:\"clusters\"`\n291: \tRoutes    ecp_v3_cache.Resources `json:\"routes\"`\n292: \tListeners ecp_v3_cache.Resources `json:\"listeners\"`\n293: \tRuntimes  ecp_v3_cache.Resources `json:\"runtimes\"`\n294: }\n295: \n296: func NewV3ExpandedSnapshot(v3snap *ecp_v3_cache.Snapshot) v3ExpandedSnapshot {\n297: \treturn v3ExpandedSnapshot{\n298: \t\tEndpoints: v3snap.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Endpoint],\n299: \t\tClusters:  v3snap.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Cluster],\n300: \t\tRoutes:    v3snap.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Route],\n301: \t\tListeners: v3snap.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Listener],\n302: \t\tRuntimes:  v3snap.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Runtime],\n303: \t}\n304: }\n305: \n306: // A combinedSnapshot has both a V2 and V3 snapshot, for logging.\n307: type combinedSnapshot struct {\n308: \tVersion string             `json:\"version\"`\n309: \tV3      v3ExpandedSnapshot `json:\"v3\"`\n310: }\n311: \n312: // csDump creates a combinedSnapshot from a V2 snapshot and a V3 snapshot, then\n313: // dumps the combinedSnapshot to disk. Only numsnaps snapshots are kept: ambex-1.json\n314: // is the newest, then ambex-2.json, etc., so ambex-$numsnaps.json is the oldest.\n315: // Every time we write a new one, we rename all the older ones, ditching the oldest\n316: // after we've written numsnaps snapshots.\n317: func csDump(ctx context.Context, snapdirPath string, numsnaps int, generation int, v3snap *ecp_v3_cache.Snapshot) {\n318: \tif numsnaps <= 0 {\n319: \t\t// Don't do snapshotting at all.\n320: \t\treturn\n321: \t}\n322: \n323: \t// OK, they want snapshots. Make a proper version string...\n324: \tversion := fmt.Sprintf(\"v%d\", generation)\n325: \n326: \t// ...and a combinedSnapshot.\n327: \tcs := combinedSnapshot{\n328: \t\tVersion: version,\n329: \t\tV3:      NewV3ExpandedSnapshot(v3snap),\n330: \t}\n331: \n332: \t// Next up, marshal as JSON and write to ambex-0.json. Note that we\n333: \t// didn't say anything about a -0 file; that's because it's about to\n334: \t// be renamed.\n335: \n336: \tbs, err := json.MarshalIndent(cs, \"\", \"  \")\n337: \n338: \tif err != nil {\n339: \t\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \"CSNAP: marshal failure: %s\", err)\n340: \t\treturn\n341: \t}\n342: \n343: \tcsPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, \"ambex-0.json\")\n344: \n345: \terr = ioutil.WriteFile(csPath, bs, 0644)\n346: \n347: \tif err != nil {\n348: \t\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \"CSNAP: write failure: %s\", err)\n349: \t} else {\n350: \t\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \"Saved snapshot %s\", version)\n351: \t}\n352: \n353: \t// Rotate everything one file down. This includes renaming the just-written\n354: \t// ambex-0 to ambex-1.\n355: \tfor i := numsnaps; i > 0; i-- {\n356: \t\tprevious := i - 1\n357: \n358: \t\tfromPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\"ambex-%d.json\", previous))\n359: \t\ttoPath := path.Join(snapdirPath, fmt.Sprintf(\"ambex-%d.json\", i))\n360: \n361: \t\terr := os.Rename(fromPath, toPath)\n362: \n363: \t\tif (err != nil) && !os.IsNotExist(err) {\n364: \t\t\tdlog.Infof(ctx, \"CSNAP: could not rename %s -> %s: %#v\", fromPath, toPath, err)\n365: \t\t}\n366: \t}\n367: }\n368: \n369: // Get an updated snapshot going.\n370: func update(\n371: \tctx context.Context,\n372: \tsnapdirPath string,\n373: \tnumsnaps int,\n374: \tedsBypass bool,\n375: \tconfigv3 ecp_v3_cache.SnapshotCache,\n376: \tgeneration *int,\n377: \tdirs []string,\n378: \tedsEndpointsV3 map[string]*v3endpointconfig.ClusterLoadAssignment,\n379: \tfastpathSnapshot *FastpathSnapshot,\n380: \tupdates chan<- Update,\n381: ) error {\n382: \n383: \tclustersv3 := []ecp_cache_types.Resource{}  // v3.Cluster\n384: \troutesv3 := []ecp_cache_types.Resource{}    // v3.RouteConfiguration\n385: \tlistenersv3 := []ecp_cache_types.Resource{} // v3.Listener\n386: \truntimesv3 := []ecp_cache_types.Resource{}  // v3.Runtime\n387: \n388: \tvar filenames []string\n389: \n390: \tfor _, dir := range dirs {\n391: \t\tfiles, err := ioutil.ReadDir(dir)\n392: \t\tif err != nil {\n393: \t\t\tdlog.Warnf(ctx, \"Error listing %q: %v\", dir, err)\n394: \t\t\tcontinue\n395: \t\t}\n396: \t\tfor _, file := range files {\n397: \t\t\tname := file.Name()\n398: \t\t\tif isDecodable(name) {\n399: \t\t\t\tfilenames = append(filenames, filepath.Join(dir, name))\n400: \t\t\t}\n401: \t\t}\n402: \t}\n403: \n404: \tfor _, name := range filenames {\n405: \t\tm, e := Decode(ctx, name)\n406: \t\tif e != nil {\n407: \t\t\tdlog.Warnf(ctx, \"%s: %v\", name, e)\n408: \t\t\tcontinue\n409: \t\t}\n410: \t\tvar dst *[]ecp_cache_types.Resource\n411: \t\tswitch m.(type) {\n412: \t\tcase *v3clusterconfig.Cluster:\n413: \t\t\tdst = &clustersv3\n414: \t\tcase *v3routeconfig.RouteConfiguration:\n415: \t\t\tdst = &routesv3\n416: \t\tcase *v3listenerconfig.Listener:\n417: \t\t\tdst = &listenersv3\n418: \t\tcase *v3runtime.Runtime:\n419: \t\t\tdst = &runtimesv3\n420: \t\tcase *v3bootstrap.Bootstrap:\n421: \t\t\tbs := m.(*v3bootstrap.Bootstrap)\n422: \t\t\tsr := bs.StaticResources\n423: \t\t\tfor _, lst := range sr.Listeners {\n424: \t\t\t\t// When the RouteConfiguration is embedded in the listener, it will cause envoy to\n425: \t\t\t\t// go through a complete drain cycle whenever there is a routing change and that\n426: \t\t\t\t// will potentially disrupt in-flight requests. By converting all listeners to use\n427: \t\t\t\t// RDS rather than inlining their routing configuration, we significantly reduce the\n428: \t\t\t\t// set of circumstances where the listener definition itself changes, and this in\n429: \t\t\t\t// turn reduces the set of circumstances where envoy has to go through that drain\n430: \t\t\t\t// process and disrupt in-flight requests.\n431: \t\t\t\trdsListener, routeConfigs, err := V3ListenerToRdsListener(lst)\n432: \t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n433: \t\t\t\t\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \"Error converting listener to RDS: %+v\", err)\n434: \t\t\t\t\tlistenersv3 = append(listenersv3, proto.Clone(lst).(ecp_cache_types.Resource))\n435: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n436: \t\t\t\t}\n437: \t\t\t\tlistenersv3 = append(listenersv3, rdsListener)\n438: \t\t\t\tfor _, rc := range routeConfigs {\n439: \t\t\t\t\t// These routes will get included in the configuration snapshot created below.\n440: \t\t\t\t\troutesv3 = append(routesv3, rc)\n441: \t\t\t\t}\n442: \t\t\t}\n443: \t\t\tfor _, cls := range sr.Clusters {\n444: \t\t\t\tclustersv3 = append(clustersv3, proto.Clone(cls).(ecp_cache_types.Resource))\n445: \t\t\t}\n446: \t\t\tcontinue\n447: \t\tdefault:\n448: \t\t\tdlog.Warnf(ctx, \"Unrecognized resource %s: %v\", name, e)\n449: \t\t\tcontinue\n450: \t\t}\n451: \t\t*dst = append(*dst, m.(ecp_cache_types.Resource))\n452: \t}\n453: \n454: \tif fastpathSnapshot != nil && fastpathSnapshot.Snapshot != nil {\n455: \t\tfor _, lst := range fastpathSnapshot.Snapshot.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Listener].Items {\n456: \t\t\tlistenersv3 = append(listenersv3, lst.Resource)\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\tfor _, route := range fastpathSnapshot.Snapshot.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Route].Items {\n459: \t\t\troutesv3 = append(routesv3, route.Resource)\n460: \t\t}\n461: \t\tfor _, clu := range fastpathSnapshot.Snapshot.Resources[ecp_cache_types.Cluster].Items {\n462: \t\t\tclustersv3 = append(clustersv3, clu.Resource)\n463: \t\t}\n464: \t\t// We intentionally omit endpoints since those are carried separately.\n465: \t}\n466: \n467: \t// The configuration data that reaches us here arrives via two parallel paths that race each\n468: \t// other. The endpoint data comes in realtime directly from the golang watcher in the entrypoint\n469: \t// package. The cluster configuration comes from the python code. Either one can win which means\n470: \t// we might at times see endpoint data with no corresponding cluster and we might also see\n471: \t// clusters with no corresponding endpoint data. Both of these circumstances should be\n472: \t// transient.\n473: \t//\n474: \t// To produce a consistent configuration we do an outer join operation on the endpoint and\n475: \t// cluster configuration that we have at this moment. If there is no endpoint information for a\n476: \t// given cluster, we will synthesize an empty ClusterLoadAssignment.\n477: \t//\n478: \t// Note that a cluster not existing is very different to envoy than a cluster existing but\n479: \t// having an empty ClusterLoadAssignment. When envoy first discovers clusters it goes through a\n480: \t// warmup process to be sure the cluster is properly bootstrapped before routing traffic to\n481: \t// it. See here for more details:\n482: \t//\n483: \t// https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/arch_overview/upstream/cluster_manager.html?highlight=cluster%20warming\n484: \t//\n485: \t// For this reason if there is no endpoint data for the cluster we will synthesize an empty\n486: \t// ClusterLoadAssignment rather than filtering out the cluster. This avoids triggering the\n487: \t// warmup sequence in scenarios where the endpoint data for a cluster is really flapping into\n488: \t// and out of existence. In that circumstance we want to faithfully relay to envoy that the\n489: \t// cluster exists but currently has no endpoints.\n490: \tendpointsv3 := JoinEdsClustersV3(ctx, clustersv3, edsEndpointsV3, edsBypass)\n491: \n492: \t// Create a new configuration snapshot from everything we have just loaded from disk.\n493: \tcurgen := *generation\n494: \t*generation++\n495: \n496: \tversion := fmt.Sprintf(\"v%d\", curgen)\n497: \n498: \tsnapshotResources := map[ecp_v3_resource.Type][]ecp_cache_types.Resource{\n499: \t\tecp_v3_resource.EndpointType: endpointsv3,\n500: \t\tecp_v3_resource.ClusterType:  clustersv3,\n501: \t\tecp_v3_resource.RouteType:    routesv3,\n502: \t\tecp_v3_resource.ListenerType: listenersv3,\n503: \t\tecp_v3_resource.RuntimeType:  runtimesv3,\n504: \t}\n505: \n506: \tsnapshot, err := ecp_v3_cache.NewSnapshot(version, snapshotResources)\n507: \tif err != nil {\n508: \t\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \"V3 Snapshot error: %v\", err)\n509: \t\treturn nil // TODO: should we return the error, rather than just logging it?\n510: \t}\n511: \n512: \tif err := snapshot.Consistent(); err != nil {\n513: \t\tbs, _ := json.Marshal(snapshot)\n514: \t\tdlog.Errorf(ctx, \"V3 Snapshot inconsistency: %v: %s\", err, bs)\n515: \t\treturn nil // TODO: should we return the error, rather than just logging it?\n516: \t}\n517: \n518: \t// This used to just directly update envoy. Since we want ratelimiting, we now send an\n519: \t// Update object down the channel with a function that knows how to do the update if/when\n520: \t// the ratelimiting logic decides.\n521: \n522: \tdlog.Debugf(ctx, \"Created snapshot %s\", version)\n523: \tcsDump(ctx, snapdirPath, numsnaps, curgen, snapshot)\n524: \n525: \tupdate := Update{version, func() error {\n526: \t\tdlog.Debugf(ctx, \"Accepting snapshot %s\", version)\n527: \n528: \t\terr = configv3.SetSnapshot(ctx, \"test-id\", snapshot)\n529: \t\tif err != nil {\n530: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"v3 Snapshot error %q for %+v\", err, snapshot)\n531: \t\t}\n532: \n533: \t\treturn nil\n534: \t}}\n535: \n536: \t// We also need to pay attention to contexts here so we can shutdown properly. If we didn't\n537: \t// have the context portion, the ratelimit goroutine could shutdown first and we could end\n538: \t// up blocking here and never shutting down.\n539: \tselect {\n540: \tcase updates <- update:\n541: \tcase <-ctx.Done():\n542: \t}\n543: \treturn nil\n544: }\n545: \n546: type logAdapterBase struct {\n547: \tprefix string\n548: }\n549: type logAdapterV3 struct {\n550:
